font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ratings in brackets, (\n), indicate insufficient data available to the GESAMP experts on specific\nsubstances, hence extrapolation was required. N \u2013 Not applicable (e.g. if\ngases) Indicates data were not available to the GESAMP Working Group.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </strong></span><strong>SHIPPING INFORMATION<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Grades or Purity</strong> - The\ngrades USP (United States Pharmacopoeia) and CP (chemically pure) are quite\npure.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Where \u201cTechnical\u201d or \u201cCommercial\u201d\ngrades are given, the percent by weight of the pure chemical present is usually\nindicated.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In a few cases the\nidentity of the major impurities is given.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>If the properties of the less pure grades differ significantly from\nthose of the pure substance, the differences in properties are described in\ngeneral terms.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Storage Temperature</strong> -\nThe range of temperatures at which the chemical is normally shipped in bulk by\nwater transport is given.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>\u201cAmbient\u201d\nmeans the temperature of the surroundings.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Inert Atmosphere</strong> - The\nterms used are \u201cinerted,\u201d \u201cpadded,\u201d \u201cventilated (forced),\u201d \u201cventilated\n(natural),\u201d and \u201cno requirement.\u201d They are given when found in the Code of\nFederal Regulations, Title 46, beginning in Part 151.05.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>IMO Pollution Category</strong>\n\u2013 pollution classification applied to this compound by the International\nMaritime Organization.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Ship Type</strong> \u2013 The data\nentry refers to construction and containment requirements for ships being used\nto transport the chemical in question.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>The information is taken from the Code of Federal Regulations, Title 46,\nPart 154.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>CHEMICAL FIRE HAZARDS<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Flash Point</strong> - This is\ndefined as the lowest temperature at which vapors above a volatile combustible\nsubstance will ignite in air when exposed to a flame.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Depending on the test method used, the values\ngiven are either Tag closed cup (C.C.) (ASTM D56) or Cleveland open cup (O.C.)\n(ASTM D93).<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The values,<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>give an indication of the relative\nflammability of the chemical.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>In\ngeneral, the open cup value is about 10o to 15oF higher than the closed cup\nvalue.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Flammable Limits in Air</strong>\n- The percent concentration in air (by volume) is given for the lower (LFL) and\nupper (UFL) limit.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The values, give an\nindication of the relative flammability of the chemical.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The limits are sometimes referred to as\n\u201clower explosive limit\u201d (LEL) and \u201cupper explosive limit\u201d (UEL).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Fire Extinguishing\nAgents Not to be Used - The agents listed must not be used because they react\nwith the chemical and create an additional hazard.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>In some cases they are listed because they\nare ineffective in putting out the fire.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Special Hazards of Combustion\nProducts</strong> - Some chemicals decompose or burn to give off toxic and irritating\ngases.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Such gases may also be given off\nby chemicals that vaporize in the heat of a fire without either decomposing or\nburning.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>If no entry appears, the\ncombustion products are thought to be similar to those formed by the burning of\noil, gasoline, or alcohol; they include carbon monoxide (poisonous), carbon\ndioxide, and water vapor.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The specific\ncombustion products are usually not well known over the wide variety of conditions\nexisting in fires; some may be hazardous.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Behavior in Fire</strong> - Any\ncharacteristic behavior that might increase significantly the hazard involved\nin a fire is described.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The formation of\ndense smoke or flammable vapor clouds, and the possibility of polymerization\nand explosions is stated.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Unusual\ndifficulty in extinguishing the fire is also noted.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Ignition Temperature</strong> -\nThis is the minimum temperature at which the material will ignite without a\nspark or flame being present.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>It gives\nan indication of the relative flammability of the chemical.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>It is sometimes called the \u201cautoignition\ntemperature.\u201d <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Electrical Hazard</strong> - The\nease with which the chemical is ignited by electrical equipment is indicated by\nthe Group and Class assignment made in the National Fire Protection\nAssociation, \u201cHazardous Chemicals Data,\u201d Boston, Mass., 1994 and in\n\u201cClassification of Gases, Liquids, and Volatile Solids Relative to\nExplosion-Proof Electrical Equipment,\u201d National Academy of Sciences, 1982.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>This information is available for relatively\nfew chemicals, so an absence of data does not necessarily mean that the\nsubstance is not hazardous in the presence of electrical equipment.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Burning Rate</strong> - The\nvalue is the rate (in millimeters per minute) at which the depth of a pool of\nliquid decreases as the liquid burns.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Adiabatic Flame\nTemperature</strong> - The value is the temperature in degrees Fahrenheit of the flame\nwhen the material is burned under adiabatic conditions.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Stoichiometric Air to\nFuel Ratio</strong> - The value is the ratio of air to the compound in question required\nfor stoichiometric combustion.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Since it\nis a ratio, the value is dimensionless.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Flame Temperature</strong> - The\nvalue is the temperature in degrees Fahrenheit of the flame produced by burning\nthe compound under stoichiometric conditions without any rate controls.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Molar Ratio (Reactant\nto Product)</strong> \u2013 The number of moles of products formed, assuming complete\ncombustion of a single mole of the chemical reactant.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>These ratios were calculated assuming there\nwas sufficient oxygen available and that combustion did, in fact, go to\ncompletion.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Minimum Oxygen\nConcentration for Combustion (MOCC)</strong> \u2013 Information from NFPA-69 regarding the\nminimum percentage of oxygen required to support combustion of the subject\ncompound.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The results are reported for\noxygen diluted with nitrogen (N2) and/or carbon dioxide (CO2).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FyKr2AzSY0Q/UBDmqLkNS7I/AAAAAAAAOGA/epLzMhdv5Ls/s1600/VADAKAYIL2.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"239\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FyKr2AzSY0Q/UBDmqLkNS7I/AAAAAAAAOGA/epLzMhdv5Ls/s320/VADAKAYIL2.JPG\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">29 years in command<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "17", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/6169217162771066470/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "6312647256895324652", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2012-07-26T00:39:00+05:30", "updated": "2013-06-25T00:38:17+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMzcyMTAwODk3OTcwCm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2012/07/unsung-heroes-of-ina-capt-ajit-vadakayil.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/6312647256895324652", "title": "UNSUNG HEROES OF INA-  CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\">\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong><span style=\"font-size: large;\"><span style=\"color: red;\">RASH BEHARI BOSE,\nAIYAPPAN PILLAI MADHAVAN NAIR , MOHAN SINGH</span>,&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style=\"color: blue;\">FOUNDER MEMBERS OF INA</span>-&nbsp; <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL</span></strong></span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<object class=\"BLOGGER-youtube-video\" classid=\"clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000\" codebase=\"http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0\" data-thumbnail-src=\"http://1.gvt0.com/vi/E9rpt4EDYVE/0.jpg\" height=\"266\" width=\"320\"><param name=\"movie\" value=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/E9rpt4EDYVE&fs=1&source=uds\" /><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#FFFFFF\" /><param name=\"allowFullScreen\" value=\"true\" /><embed width=\"320\" height=\"266\"  src=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/E9rpt4EDYVE&fs=1&source=uds\" type=\"application/x-shockwave-flash\" allowfullscreen=\"true\"></embed></object></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"color: red; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p><em>Play the video above in low volume, while reading this post.&nbsp; You must know what selflessness and love for the motherland is all about.</em></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-PAdySApQT8Y/UBBCaGFJ5YI/AAAAAAAAODA/QUQbJM22yMo/s1600/335841.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-PAdySApQT8Y/UBBCaGFJ5YI/AAAAAAAAODA/QUQbJM22yMo/s1600/335841.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"color: blue; font-size: large;\">Let me re-write some Indian history-- let me exhume some unsung heroes .</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Rash Behari Bose and Nair San, are Indians with Japanese wives. These two\nare the real force behind INA--never mind the propaganda of the Subhash Chandra\nBose cheerleaders . <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">INA was handed over to\nNetaji Subhash Chandra Bose on a platter by the Japanese when Captain Mohan\nSingh and RB Bose disbanded INA , as the Indian soldiers were suspicious of the real\nmotives of the Japan, was to wrest india from Britain, and to use the INA\nsoldiers as coolies for cheap hard labour,<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>which snooty Japanese soldiers did NOT want to do.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">To revive INA Subhash\nChandra Bose was called urgently requisitioned by the Japanese Prime Minister.&nbsp; Subhash\nChandra Bose was in Germany at that time having married a Jewish woman with whom he produced a daughter&nbsp;. </span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">SC Bose was put on a German U-180 &nbsp;submarine and transferred to a\nI-29 Japanese submarine off Madagascar and taken to Japan for parleys with the\nJapanese Prime Minister. And then he arrived at Singapore in Field Marshall's uniform , to take over INA.&nbsp; Talk about easy promotions in the military, for doing nothing.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">See no matter how much\nBCCI and Lalit Modi tries to claim credit for original thinkin of IPL--this\nformat was the brainchild of ICL of Zee TV.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\nSame way INA cannot be cedited to Subhash Chandra Bose.</span><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Let me first talk about\nthe unsung Bengali Indian Rash Behari Bose-- a great Indian patriot.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Rash Behari Bose<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>was born on 25 May 1886 at<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Subaldaha village, Burdwan Dist., West\nBengal, India.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He initiated the Ghadar\nConspiracy that attempted to trigger a mutiny in India as early as February 1915.\nTrusted and tried Ghadarites were sent to several cantonments to infiltrate into\nthe British army. The idea of the RB Bose&nbsp;was that with the war raging in\nEurope most of the soldiers had gone out of India and the rest could be easily\nwon over. The revolution failed and most of the revolutionaries were arrested.\nBut Rash Behari managed to escape British intelligence and reached Japan in\n1915.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">RB Bose&nbsp;was the brain child\nof the failed attempt and conspiracy to assassinate Lord Hardinge. Rash Behari was forced\nto go into hiding. He was hunted by the colonial police due to his active\nparticipation in bomb throwing&nbsp;at the Governor\nGeneral and Viceroy Lord Charles Hardinge in Delhi (the bomb was actually\nthrown by Basanta Kumar Biswas, a disciple of Amarendra Chatterjee)<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">After throwing the\nbomb, Bose managed to escape arrest and went in hiding in Varanasi. With the\nhelp of the members of the Ghadar Party, he planned a simultaneous rebellion\nwhich would rock the whole of north India. The British, however, foiled all\nattempts of Bose to create unrest and arrested several of Bose's confidants; of\nwhich twenty- eight were hanged after trials under what came to be known as the\nLahore Conspiracy Case. </span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">There was a prize of Rs.7,500 on his head. His pictures\nwere posted in all public places.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>RB\nBose managed to escape from India in 1915 and went to Japan where he lived as a\nfugitive. He<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>came to Saharanpur where\nBarrister J.M. Chatterji raised some money from his friends for his voyage to\nJapan. From Saharanpur, Rash Behari came back to Chandernagar from where he\nescaped to Japan under the assumed name of Raja P.N. Tagore, on a British passport--as a relative of Rabinndra Nath Tagore.</span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In June 1915, Rash\nBehari reached Tokyo. He convened there a meeting of the sponsors of the Indian\nFreedom Movement, in the famous 'Sayoken' Hotel on 25th November, 1915.\n Besides reputed revolutionaries and the Japanese sympathizers, the meeting was\nalso attended by the Punjab Lion, Lala Lajpat Rai. The meeting aroused awareness&nbsp;of the Japanese people about India and&nbsp;the efforts of the freedomfighters and revolutionaries. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">From 1915\u20131918, RB Bose\nchanged residences and identities numerous times, as the British kept pressing\nthe Japanese government for his extradition. He married the daughter of Soma\nAizo and Soma Kotsuko, the owner of Nakamuraya restaurant in Tokyo&nbsp;in 1918 and became a Japanese citizen ( with an Indian heart ) in 1923, living as a\njournalist and writer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">But in pursuance of the\nconditions of the Anglo-Japanese alliance, the Japanese Government was forced\nto direct Rash Behari and his associate, Herambalal Gupta, to leave the shores\nof Japan before the 2nd of December. &nbsp;However, the Japanese people and the press\ncame out openly supporting Rash Behari. The elderly political leader, Mitsui\nToyama, assured help and protection to Rash Behari. Mr. Aizo Zoma, a man of\nfortune and owner of the most reputed Japanese Hotel, 'Naka Muraya', negotiated\nwith Mr. Toyama through Mr. Naka Mura, Editor of Niroku, and provided secret\nhiding for Rash Behari in the cellar of the influential hotel. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">During his stay in\n'Naka Muraya', Mr. and Mrs. Zoma, who bestowed on him loving care, developed a\nfilial affection for Rash Behari. They offered their eldest daughter, Tosiko,\nin marriage to Rash Behari. The couple had two children Masahide a boy, and a\n Tetaku a girl.&nbsp; Tosiko died at the age of 28, in March 1928 .</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-bUAh8j_WNAY/UBBJ8JthypI/AAAAAAAAOEw/XoWoIyIXmd0/s1600/imagesCA21MSCY.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-bUAh8j_WNAY/UBBJ8JthypI/AAAAAAAAOEw/XoWoIyIXmd0/s1600/imagesCA21MSCY.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">As soon as the Second World War broke out,\nRash Behari Bose found another great opportunity to make an attempt to liberate\nhis Motherland. On 15th February 1942, Singapore fell into the hands of Japan.\nOn that day 15,000 British, 13,000 Australian and 32,000 Indian soldiers were\nthere in Singapore, and all of them were taken as prisoners of war by the\nJapanese. Japan also took over Malaya and established her authority over the\ncountry of fifty lakhs of people, among whom three lakhs were Indians.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-grjuALaTHrM/UBBKBIU36bI/AAAAAAAAOE4/MIlgyKmlnAY/s1600/images.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-grjuALaTHrM/UBBKBIU36bI/AAAAAAAAOE4/MIlgyKmlnAY/s1600/images.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\"></span>A brilliant idea crossed across the mind of\nRash Behari Bose, about forming a&nbsp;Liberation Army to&nbsp;invade\nIndia and fight the British ,from outside. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Major\nFujihara, a Japanese officer, used his interpreter Giani&nbsp;Pritam Singh and requested Mohan Singh to form an Indian Army\ncomprising the captured Indian soldiers. Mohan Singh hesitated but ultimately\nagreed.. Fujihara handed over about 40,000 Indian soldiers, who had surrendered\nto him, to Mohan Singh. It was actually the first step towards the formation of\nthe INA.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-_87obnKWOrU/UBBKkNQ8a1I/AAAAAAAAOFA/asWAJlYm6XA/s1600/imagesCAYAU14J.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-_87obnKWOrU/UBBKkNQ8a1I/AAAAAAAAOFA/asWAJlYm6XA/s1600/imagesCAYAU14J.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">So, on February 15, 1942\nthe Indian National Army (INA) was formed by Captain Mohan Singh. In addition\nto the INA was the India Independence League which was headed by Rashbehari\nBose. Other leaders included Kesava (KPK) Menon who was the political guru and\nSC Guha. There were military officers in it from the INA.</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;They all went to\nTokyo to meet the Japanese government and get assurances from them that the INA\nwould be given the status of an allied army. Unfortunately, the Japanese only\nverbally agreed to this but never officially ratified them. This was the reason\nwhy Mohan Singh and Kesava Menon feeling they could not trust the Japanese and\nMohan Singh decided to disband the INA. Mohan Singh was subsequently arrested\nby the Japanese on Dec 29th 1942, and exiled to Pulau Ubin. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-QA0eQvJ4V-k/UBBKp80uzEI/AAAAAAAAOFI/J_VQMSKlmqY/s1600/imagesCAMVGHIC.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-QA0eQvJ4V-k/UBBKp80uzEI/AAAAAAAAOFI/J_VQMSKlmqY/s1600/imagesCAMVGHIC.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">RB Bose along with A M\nNair was instrumental in persuading the Japanese authorities to stand by the\nIndian nationalists and ultimately to support actively the Indian freedom\nstruggle abroad. RB Bose convened a conference in Tokyo on 28\u201330 March 1942,\nwhich decided to establish the Indian Independence League. At the conference he\nmoved a motion to raise an army for Indian liberation.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-C7MwMi8a77I/UciY0DSvLAI/AAAAAAAAjfc/WSYVAmsHmuQ/s1600/Indian+revolutionary+leader+Rash+Behari+Bose+with+his+Japanese+Wife+Toshiko+(1).jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"400\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-C7MwMi8a77I/UciY0DSvLAI/AAAAAAAAjfc/WSYVAmsHmuQ/s400/Indian+revolutionary+leader+Rash+Behari+Bose+with+his+Japanese+Wife+Toshiko+(1).jpg\" width=\"270\" /></a></div>\n<b><i><span style=\"color: red;\"><br /></span></i></b>\n<b><i><span style=\"color: red;\">Above : Rash Behari Bose with Jap wife Toshiko.</span></i></b><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">From June 14 to 23\n1942, a second conference of Indians was held in the East in Bangkok.\nRepresentatives of about three lakhs of Indians scattered all over Java,\nSumatra, Indo-China, Borneo, Manchuko, Hongkong, Burma, Malaya and Japan had\ngathered in large numbers. The conference presented a memorandum to Japan\nrequesting that its demand for equal rights and status for the Azad Hind Fauz\nof Free India be conceded. The meeting also constituted the War Council of the\nLeague with Rash Behari Bose as the first President and Mr. M. Raghavan, K.R.K.\nMenon, Captain Mohan Singh and Colonel G.K. Gillani as other members. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Indian prisoners of\nwar captured by the Japanese in the Malaya and Burma fronts were encouraged to\njoin the Indian Independence League and become the soldiers of the Indian\nNational Army (INA), formed on 1 September 1942 as the military wing of Bose's\nIndian National League. RB Bose&nbsp;selected the flag called as Azad .<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In 1940, our hero Netaji Subhash Chandra Bose&nbsp;was imprisoned by the British\nfor his anti-colonial activities. While in prison in India , Bose went on a hunger\nstrike. The British put him under house arrest. He subsequently escaped to\nGermany through Afghanistan by pretending to be a deaf-mute Pathan. Bose\nreached Berlin on 2 April 1941, where he began advocating India\u2019s Independence\nthrough radio broadcasts.</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-bm3cN8OrWF4/UBBDCsmGqxI/AAAAAAAAODI/qFzrlPkfoWc/s1600/photo.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-bm3cN8OrWF4/UBBDCsmGqxI/AAAAAAAAODI/qFzrlPkfoWc/s1600/photo.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In January 1943, the\nJapanese invited SC Bose to lead the Indian nationalist movement in East Asia.\nHe accepted and left Germany on 8 February. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-L8A34AuF7M0/UBBDJPFu66I/AAAAAAAAODQ/VVQdLfFQM94/s1600/Greater_East_Asia_Conference.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-L8A34AuF7M0/UBBDJPFu66I/AAAAAAAAODQ/VVQdLfFQM94/s1600/Greater_East_Asia_Conference.JPG\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Subhash Chandra Bose left for Japan\nin a German submarine , and hopped on to a Japanese submarine midsea off Madagascar and arrived in Tokyo on 13 June 1943. Hideki Tojo, the\nJapanese Prime Minister (1941-44), accorded him a cordial reception on his\narrival. The Prime Minister declared in their parliament that Japan would\nadvance all sorts of help to India in its fight for independence. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In Tokyo, SC Bose made\na number of radio broadcasts to the Indian communities and exhorted them to\njoin in the fight for India\u2019s Independence. </span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\nSC Bose reached&nbsp;<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Tokyo\nby Japanese submarine&nbsp;on June 20.&nbsp; On July 2, he reached Singapore where the Indians,\nChinese and the Japanese accorded him an unprecedented welcome. Addressing a\nmammoth gathering, he gave the call to Indians\u2014\"Chalo Delhi\" (march\non to Delhi).</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Pqq5LOwudFo/UBBD2ovZTBI/AAAAAAAAODw/NBzCzw-X89U/s1600/untitledxvn.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"212\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Pqq5LOwudFo/UBBD2ovZTBI/AAAAAAAAODw/NBzCzw-X89U/s320/untitledxvn.png\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On July 5, 1943, Rash Behari Bose officially conferred on Subhash Bose the\nPresidentship of Indian Independence League ( as per Japanese wish ) and constituted himself as his\nadviser. Soon under the captaincy of Laxmi Sehgal , the Rani Laxmi Regiment was formed.\n</span><br />\n<br />\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On 25th August, 1943, Subhash assumed the Supreme Command of the Free Indian\nNational Army.<o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On 21 October 1943, SC\nBose announced the formation of the Provisional Government of Azad Hind (Free\nIndia), with himself as the Head of State, Prime Minister and Minister of War.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Mohan Singh was NOT\nreinstated to the INA--which showed the real worth of Netaji Bose.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Netaji wanted money. Many Indian civilians\nfrom Malaya, Thailand and Burma responded enthusiastically. They contributed\nmoney and gold generously to the INA Fund. The gold came mostly from women who\nreadily gave up their jewellery while wealthy Indian families donated large\nsums of money after attending Bose\u2019s rallies and meetings. Other forms of\ncontributions included clothing, foodstuffs and other supplies that the INA\ncould use.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">At the huge rally\norganized by the Indian Independence League at Singapore to welcome Netaji, he\nsudenly announced that he would like to auction the garlands that had been put\naround his neck. \u201cThe bid started with Rs 1 lakh (in 1943 it was more than\nrupees fifty lakh of today). The first garland was auctioned for Rs 1 crore and\n3 lakh, which was purchased by a Muslim industrialist of Malaya, Habibur\nRehman. He also volunteered his services to join the movement.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Indian women selflessly offered their\ngold ornaments. Total collections at this auction were about Rs\n25 crore --a king's ransom those days.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">By April 1944, the Azad\nHind Bank was established in Rangoon to manage the overwhelming donations from\nthe Indian communities. <span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Abid Hasan Safrani coined the salutation \"Jai Hind\" (Hail India). <o:p></o:p></span><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It was decided that\nonly a regiment of the Indian soldiers would take part in the fight with the\nJapanese as a detached unit. If they could prove themselves equal to the\nJapanese, more Indians would be permitted to march to the border. A new brigade\nnamed Subhash Brigade was formed with select soldiers from the erstwhile Gandhi,\nAzad and Nehru Brigades. The rest were shipped off to Rabaul to dig tunnels -- a deception most foul, by the Japanese.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The army after\ntraining, started their advance towards India from Burma and had even reached\nImphal town on Indian soil. They were however beaten back by the British\nsoldiers afterwords. The INA later collapsed and Subhash Chandra Bose\ndisappeared from the political scene mysteriously. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Netaji Subhas Chandra\nBose arrived from from Saigon on, August 23, 1945 at\nDairen (Manchuria) at 1:30 PM.. This was was a Japanese bomber\nplane. &nbsp;It was full of gold in the shape of bars, Indian ornaments and jewelry.&nbsp; &nbsp;Netaji\ncarried two attache cases, one in each hand.&nbsp; On alighting from the plane,\nNetaji took tea with bananas.&nbsp; When Netaji finished tea, he along with four\nothers, out of which one was a Japanese named General Shidei climbed into a&nbsp;jeep standing nearby and proceeded toward Russian territory.\n After about 3 hours the&nbsp; jeep returned and informed the waiting pilot of the plane\nwho flew back to Tokyo.</span><br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\nNetaji Subhash Chandra Bose was never seen again. He resurfaced in India and lived for many years as a Mauni (Silent ) Baba behind a curtain.&nbsp; He had done this fancy dress thing before, as a dumb and deaf Pathan,&nbsp; and was in familiar territory.<br />\n<br />\n<br />\nNetaji did NOT want the fate of Hideki Tojo, the Prime Minister of Japan who was hung to death. <br />\n<br />\n<br />\nHe also did NOT have the courage to face his own men of INA, who were fooled into digging tunnels at Rabaul.&nbsp; He had also told them a big lie that since he did NOT have children every soldier of INA was his child. They gave him blood and in return he betrayed their trust.<br />\n<br />\n<br />\nRead my post by punching into Google search<strong> <span style=\"color: red;\">NETAJI SUBHASH</span><span style=\"color: red;\"> CHANDRA BOSE, UNTOLD SECRETS OF RABAUL TUNNELS- VADAKAYIL</span> </strong>and be shocked.<br />\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">RB Bose had great\norganizational skill and a wonderful spirit of sacrifice. Hardly anybody knows\n</span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On 21st January, 1945,\nRash Behari died of heart attack at Tokyo. He was cremated by the Buddhist rites and his\nashes were buried in Yama Cemetery. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Prior to being killed\nnear the end of World War II, the Japanese Government honoured RB Bose<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>with the Order of the Rising Sun (2nd grade).\n</span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">But the honour done by\nthe Emperor of Japan on his demise is more touching. The Imperial coach was\nsent to carry the dead body of the Indian veteran revolutionary. In 1959, when\nthe ashes of Rash Behari were brought to India by his daughter, Tetsu Higuchi,\nDr. Rajendra Prasad, the then President of India, paid to the noble son of\nBharat a glowing tribute in which he said, \"Rash Behari Bose was one of\nthose well-known patriots whose love for the Motherland and burning desire to\nsee her free could never be curbed.\"<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong><span style=\"color: blue;\">MOHAN SINGH</span></strong>-- He was\nborn the only son of Tara Singh and Hukam Kaur, a peasant couple of Ugoke\nvillage, near Sialkot (now in Pakistan). <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-eHmbpFiTrFU/UBBDXVVcY4I/AAAAAAAAODY/_Ele2ajLgf4/s1600/1327126106_rash%2520behari%2520bose%2520one.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">At the Indian Military\nAcademy, Dehra Dun, he received his commission in 1934 and was posted for a\nyear to a British unit, the 2nd Border Regiment, and then to 1st Battalion of\nhis former 14th Punjab Regiment, which at that time happened to be at Jhelum.\nWorld War II broke out in 1939.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-eaLV4XSx1lU/UBBEBAOv0OI/AAAAAAAAOD4/1HLIK2GavNU/s1600/sg.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"240\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-eaLV4XSx1lU/UBBEBAOv0OI/AAAAAAAAOD4/1HLIK2GavNU/s320/sg.png\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; However, due to public pressure, roused by the INA Red Fort\ntrials, Mohan Singh was only cashiered from the Army. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-7WfVSpqoqwQ/UBBDdUpsNsI/AAAAAAAAODg/IpM4SDNpxdw/s1600/imagesfjk;.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; You must understand that these diameters were calculated more thas 6 millenniums ago when even the atmospheric refraction of earth was different.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"color: blue;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"color: red;\">Much before Pythagoras came to India and stole his theorem.</span><br />\n<span style=\"color: blue; font-size: large;\"><br /></span>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Maya is mentioned 23\ntimes in the Ramayana, and 61 times in the Mahabharata.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>A unique reason for glory and legacy indeed.\nHe was the acharya of all the Mayavis ( sorcerers ).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Maya Danava was a\ndescendant of Danu, one of Kasyapa\u2018s 13 wives and a daughter of Dakhsa\nPrajapati.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Maya Danava was in the\nKhandava forest,&nbsp; at the outskirts of New\nDelhi,&nbsp; to build for Takshaka the Naga\nking.&nbsp; This was the opportunity Arjuna in\ncollusion with Lord Krishna looked for. They set fire to the mighty forest\nwhich was reputed to hold every specimen of flora and fauna. In this gruesome\ndeliberate fire everything died except Takshaka's Aswasena son and 4 sarnagaka\nbirds.&nbsp; Maya was conveniently saved by\nLord Krishna.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br /></span>\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-wuwwI4Jy3a8/UA55yqlm92I/AAAAAAAAN-E/WKhSoks8WfQ/s1600/imagesCATYT594.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-wuwwI4Jy3a8/UA55yqlm92I/AAAAAAAAN-E/WKhSoks8WfQ/s1600/imagesCATYT594.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Out of sheer gratitude\nAsura Maya Danava asked , how he can ever repay Arjuna. Immediately Lord\nKrishna trapped him.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>\"Let a\npalatial Sabha (meeting hall) as thou choosest, be built by thee, if thou, O\nson of Diti, who art the foremost of all artists, desirest to do good to\nYudhishthira the just (Mbh.2.1)\". <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-x5bIYkJiwJU/UA57JGjvhpI/AAAAAAAAN-M/dATAJwtWNCA/s1600/imagesCAZKGNSJ.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"318\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-x5bIYkJiwJU/UA57JGjvhpI/AAAAAAAAN-M/dATAJwtWNCA/s320/imagesCAZKGNSJ.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Krishna told Arjuna\n\"Your city has been constructed by Vishwakarma and is truly beautiful.\nHowever, the Indraprastha palace is much too plain for such a wonderful city.\nLet a palatial meeting hall be constructed for Yudhishtra the just. Maya Danava\nis the best person to construct it, being the architect of the\nAsuras.\"Maya measured out a plot of land five thousand cubits square and\nbegan the construction. Soon the peerless palace of great beauty encrusted with\ndiamonds was completed. The columns of this palace were made of gold. Maya\nappointed 8000 asuras called Kinkaras to guard this palace. Inside the palace,\nthere were many amazing devices. It took the Maya just fourteen months to\ncomplete this building. Everything was made as per the principles of Vaastu.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In Indian history,\nMayan appears several times, most significantly as the author of Mayamatam,\n\"Concept of Mayan\" which is a Vastu Shastra, a text on art,\narchitecture and town planning. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Narada on hearing of\nthis palace hall came to visit , and he cried \"O Child, I have never seen\nnor heard ever before, neither among men, nor among the gods, any assembly room\nbuilt of gems and precious stones like this hall of thine. I have been to the\nhall of Indra, it is not equal to yours. I have been to the hall of Yama that shines\nlike burnished gold, but it is inferior to this hall in beauty. I have visited\nPushakaramalini, the hall of Varuna, floating in the waters, but it is not\nequal to yours. The hall of Kubera certainly displays his immense wealth, but\nis not as beautiful as yours. I have been to the hall of Lord Brahma, the\ngrandsire of all beings, where the Prajapatis offer him worship, but its\nsplendor is nothing to yours. I have seen all these assembly halls O King, but\nwithout question, your hall is the best that ever was.\"<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In India, even modern\narchitects learn Maya Danava's Vaastu as part of their syllabus. They perceive\nexistence in terms of two dimensions: first the infinite spiritual realm and\nsecond the finite accommodating space for insentient material objects. This concept\nof a superior plane of existence, where the original form of things exist\neternally, is the basis of India's sacred architecture. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vaastu shastra\nprescribes desirable characteristics for sites and buildings based on flow of\nenergy called Vaastu Purusha.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vaastu Shastra which is\nconsidered a conduit between man and nature is based on the infinite powers of\nthe five elements \u2013 fire, water, earth, and air and space. It essentially deals\nwith two energy sources \u2013 the solar energy flux and the geomagnetic energy\nflux. This science aims at controlling the flow of these two energies by\nselecting proper directions and alignments for the vaastu. Vaastu is basically\naimed at harnessing the higher energy levels within the self and can help in\nvarious aspects of life. Buildings not constructed as per Vaastu see their\ndecline to ruins much faster than those built otherwise.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">I will get back to the\nscience of Vaastu later on. Vaastu is an Indian thing. You have to be VERY\nsurprised when the intricate mathematical and geometrical principles are Vaastu\nare followed in arhitecture abroad, when all civilizations were wide apart.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Now let me get back to\nthe surprising similarities between Indian civilisations and these South and\nCentral American civilizations. This first Indian contact happened 11000 years\nago.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yQYwcfAxz6E/UA54dlVmlKI/AAAAAAAAN9E/QPTCD7xpfJ4/s1600/images.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"305\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yQYwcfAxz6E/UA54dlVmlKI/AAAAAAAAN9E/QPTCD7xpfJ4/s400/images.jpg\" width=\"400\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The ancient Mexican\ngame of Patolli is similar in details to the game of Panchisi played in India.\nThe mathematical probability of two games invented separately agreeing by\nchance in so many specific intricate features, is zilch.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Mexican call a potter \"Kumbhar\",\nas Sanskrit word. There are several other similarities.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">After Vedic people the\nMayas of Yucatan were the first people to use a zero sign in Mathematics. This knowledge came from India, as we had this knowledge thousand of years before them. &nbsp;</span><span style=\"background-color: #fafafa; font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">All\nover Mayan civilization you find stone sculptures of Indian Vimanas and people in space suits. They just\nsculpted what they saw. &nbsp;The Kundalini snake of Lord Shiva is also depicted.</span><br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"background: #fafafa; font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<span style=\"background-color: #fafafa; font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 115%;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The elephant on a\nsculptured pillar at Copan, which he referred to as an \u201cidol\u201d. Is an animal\nunknown in that country. It is an Indian elephant and NOT an African elephant.\nIndian elephants are found in Indian elephants as they are conscious creatures.\nThey can see their image in the mirror, which only humans can do. Animals and\nbirds cant see themselves in the mirror.</span><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Few like Bonobos and Chimps can see partially.</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3Mkvkloo_wo/UA52Fh1AY7I/AAAAAAAAN74/DQwFnGR7fVQ/s1600/imagesCA3KWS4A.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"640\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3Mkvkloo_wo/UA52Fh1AY7I/AAAAAAAAN74/DQwFnGR7fVQ/s640/imagesCA3KWS4A.jpg\" width=\"502\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Archaeologists found\nmany Hindu deities like Shiva, black meteorite Shiva linga, Lord Ganesha,\nGoddess Kali, Sun god Surya , Buddha etc. (in similar or slightly different\nforms) which were worshiped in ancient America.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Images of Ganesha have been excavated in\nplenty in Mexico. This amazing piece of stone disc is 12 feet in diameter and weights\nmore than 20 tons.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">A festival called\nSita-Ram (Situa - Raimi) was celebrated in Mexico during Nav-Ratri or Dussehra\nperiod which has been described on page 5867 in the book 'Hamsworth History of\nthe World'.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Both in Central and South\nAmerica, there are found cremation, priesthood, gurukul system, yajna,\nbirth, marriage and death ceremonies to some extent similar to the Hindus.
